H O W  T O  C O N N E C T  T H E  P H Y S I C A L 
A N D  T H E  D I G I T A L ?
I N P U T  -  O U T P U T  B R A I N S T O R M 
The team is brainstorming on which inputs are 
significant to the robot and what outputs must come 
out of it. This may create a focus on the functions and 
put design in second row but ensure that the needed 
functions are viable and let the team discuss the 
importance of these.
H O W  T O  C R E A T E  A  H O L I S T I C 
C O N C E P T ?
D E S I G N I N G  A  C A R T O O N 
C H A R A C T E R 
The team is asked to design a cartoon character instead 
of a robot. This might make the task more tangible 
and open up to new possibilities. The idea is that a 
robot might look too much as a robot, while a cartoon 
character is a more open platform and it may look as 
anything and certain features may be exaggerated. 
A l t e r n a t i v e s :
•	
Base the character on some famous/known 
character; What would Jesus do?

animation looking at movements in decided situations 
and make the robot more ”alive” and thereby more 
cherished by the user.

C O N C E P T ?
C O N S T R A I N S 
Put up constraints for the looks. e.g. Must not have 
straight lines, must look like a cat, etc.
F U N C T I O N  A N A LY S I S 
Function surfaces, touch points etc. to ensure the 
functionality and see where freedoms can be taken as 
the designer.
M O O D B O A R D 
Create a moodboard to simulate the feeling and 
intentions of the robotic look.
S K E T C H I N G 
As the title suggests.
H O W  T O  C R E A T E  N O V E L  I D E A S ? 
C O N S T R A I N S 
See previous explanation.
I P A D  K E Y B O A R D  O R 
“ R Y T M E K A S S E N ” 
Digital or physical box of instruments create an 
inspirational plug and play solution for prototyping robot 
sounds.
D O G M A S 
Creating a strict set of rules to help the creative 
process along. This could be dogmas about specific 
sensors, physical appearance or restrictions for the use 
process. This could help the designer create stronger 
communicative tools in each of the three domains. 
A l t e r n a t i v e s :
•	
Either the rules can be strictly applied for the 
robot to create a more holistic expression and a 
”cleaner” communication of the functions of the 
robot. Ex. ”the robot should not look like a Sci-Fi 
character”
•	
Brainstorming with restrictions so that the 
ideas can only use one of the three dimensions 
or functionalities. This could help the 
designers be more creative and strengthen 
the communicative skill within each of the 
dimensions.
N E G A T I V E  S O U N D  B R A I N S T O R M 
Brainstorm on ”Which sounds should NOT be imple- 
mented in the robot” to create a better understanding 
of which should. And at the same time open up for 
creative environment.
D I S T O R T  Y O U R  O W N  V O I C E 
Distort a taping of your own voice to get the intonation 
right. inspired from mother’s speaking with their babies.
E L E C T R O D E S  O N  D A N C E R S /A C T O R S 
See previous explanation.
P U P P E T S 
Use hand puppets to create an interaction between user 
and robot. This is a way to pretotype through the ”eyes 
of a child”. This may create a more open and non-
conservative discussion.
Test sounds to a certain interaction Put different sounds 
to a certain interaction to see which are wrong and 
which are right.

D . 1 . 3   T E S T
H O W  T O  T E S T  I N T E R A C T I O N S 
Q U I C K LY ?
S T O P  M O T I O N  M O V I E S 
A prototyping concept that makes interaction situations 
more real in a cheap and customizable way.
3 D  A N I M A T I O N 
A prototyping concept that makes interaction situations 
more real in a cheap and customizable way. Demands 
more resources but creates a more realistic version than 
the one above. Can also be used as communication with 
customers.

T H E  F O L LO W I N G  A R E  A  C O N C E P T U A L I S AT I O N  O F  8  O F  T H E  I D E A S  F R O M  T H E 
I D E AT I O N  P H A S E . 
The 8 were each scaled within the areas of:
•	
TIME EFFICIENCY: How long time would it take to complete the method com- pared to the quality of the 
outcome.
•	
PREREQUISITES ALREADY ON TEAM: To what degree would the teams working with these tasks have the 
necessary skills to use the method.
•	
COST AND INVESTMENT: How much would it cost to execute the method and how big would the investments 
needed to start up be.
•	
NOVELTY: How novel is the method in the world of design, HRI and HCI.
•	
Integration in environment: How easy would it be for the intended users of the method to accept it based on 
their current company culture.
•	
LEARNABILITY: How easy would it be to learn to use the method for the first time.
•	
Effectiveness: How great could the expected outcome of the method be.
•	
FLEXIBILITY: To what degree could the method be used in a variety of different projects.
•	
PROJECT FEASIBILITY: To what degree would it be realistic for us to test the method out within the scope of 
this project.
CONCEPTUALISATION

A 6 8   |  A P P E N D I X  E  -  C O N C E P T U A L I S AT I O N
Concept No.  1
Inspired from Context
Date: 05.11.2015
Description
The design team would be shown pictures, video and tape recordings from the context. From this inspiration they would be asked to do 3 
brainstorms. 
- One where pictures from the context would be the inspiration for a brainstorm on the visual appearance of the robot. 
- One where video from the context would be the inspiration for a brainstorm on the movements of the robot. The video could be e.i. a recording 
of certain how the problems are solved currently.
- One where tape recordings from the context would be the inspiration for a brainstorm on the sounds of the robot.
Purpose
The purpose of the method is to create robotic concepts that ﬁt the context the robot is needed in. Using the method will ensure that the ﬁnished 
robot can be integrated in the environment without causing frictions. The method would be used early in the design process. After needs are 
identiﬁed, but before there is a general concept for the robot. The output of the method is ideas focusing on each of the three dimensions sound, 
motion and visual appearance of the robot. The ideas could be in the form of text, sketches, sound ﬁles or mock-ups.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
The method will put the designers mind set in the context of the user by providing inspiration from that environment. It is common understand-
ing that the inspiration provided will inﬂuence the resulting ideas in deisgn. With a starting point in the use context the ideas generated will be 
tied to that context in some way or another. Conduction the 3 brainstorms will force the design team to think of all three aspects or the robot and 
not just the one they usually work with.
Additional thoughts
Instruments or a digital synthesiser could be used during brainstorm on sounds. Storyboarding and mock-ups could be used during brainstorm 
of movements.
-
+
Time efﬁcient
Prerequisites already on team?
Costs and investments
Novelty (Design, HRI, HCI)
Integration in environment (Culture)

Effectiveness
Flexibility (Can be used in many different projects)

D E V E LO P M E N T  O F  T O O L B OX  C O N TA I N I N G  M E T H O D S  F O R  H R I  D E S I G N   |   A 69
Concept No.  2
Puppeteer
Date: 05.11.2015
Description
The design team is asked to choose a living being as the source of their inspiration for the robot. This should be a being they wish to let their robot 
be associated with. They are then asked to deﬁne the characteristics of the living being with respect to sound, movement and visual appearance 
(imitate). When the characteristics have been identiﬁed the team is asked to simplify them down to their core. The last stage is about exagerating 
the simpliﬁed characteristics. The exagerated characteristics can thereafter be incorporated into the robot.
Purpose
The purpose of this method is to induce more life-like elements in robots in their sound, movements and visual appearance to enhance accept-
ance by their users. The method would be used in the early stages of concept development for the robot. After context and needs have been 
identiﬁed, but before a general concept has been chosen. It could also be used as an add on, during the design process to adjust an existing 
design in the direction of a more life-like entity. The output is speciﬁc design suggestions for sound, movements and visual appearance inspired 
from living beings.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
It is easier to be inspired from an actual living being than comming up with ideas for sound, movement and visual appearance out of the blue 
that is suppose to make a robot more life-like. Inspired from a method used by puppeteers, this is a way to identify core aspects of behavior and 
use it in exagerated form to enduce life into robots. Simply copying the characteristics directly might not be possible or enough to make the robot 
seem alive.
Additional thoughts
Maybe a tool that could distort the voice of the chosen living being could be useful in simplifying and exagerating sound. Animation principles 
could be equally useful conserning movement. A concern could be the step of going from exageration to the robot, how does that work?
-
+
Time efﬁcient
Prerequisites already on team?

A 7 0   |  A P P E N D I X  E  -  C O N C E P T U A L I S AT I O N
Concept No.  3
Robotic Persona
Date: 05.11.2015
Description
The Robotic Persona is similar to the well-known method of Personas, but instead of estimating the pesonal traits of the stakeholders it is here 
used to build up the character of the designed robot. The design team uses a Robotic Persona template to ﬁll out information about the robot they 
are about to design. The headlines on the template guides the discussion an makes sure a holistic character is created. 
The headlines are: ???
When faced with a design decision later on in the process the Robotic Persona is used by asking; “what would our Robotic Persona do in this 
situation?” This could on questions such as speed, behavior, feedback, visual features etc.
Purpose
The purpose of the Robotic Persona method is to create a holistic plan for the design of the robot. The idea is that the desired characteristics of the 
robot are deﬁned as a base for further design decisions. These are non-tangible traits of the robot, focused more on the personality. The method 
can be used by designers wishing to communicate an overall goal with the robot concept. The method should be used in the early stages of 
design. After the context and needs are deﬁned, but before a general concept has been formed. The output is a document that can be revisited at 
any stage of the design process to guide design decisions.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
The method helps the design team see the robot as an autonomous actor as their users instead of a passive product. This will help them create an 
intensional design, and not accidental personality traits. It creates a overall plan with the design. Instead of making decisions on a problem basis 
the method will provide an overall guideline for the design. This can be especially helpful to design teams with changing members.
Additional thoughts
Alternatively the method could be guided by archetype characters as inspiration. What should the headlines be? How to make it more extensive? I 
could be considered to give one person the responsibility of having the task to make sure it is integrated in every design decision.
-
+
Time efﬁcient

Concept No.  4
Scenario simulation
Date: 5. november 2015
Purpose
Help you in design of interaction, as a creative tool to get you to think through the interactive scenarios in the robots and users life. Helps you 
integrate best practice concepts from theory in movement, sound and appearance. The objective is to come around all the dimensions in a playful 
setup. Can be used in the analysis phase of a project to further understand the needs of the user or in a later test phase to test interaction 
scenarios designed.
Short description
In a reinactment of an interaction between human and a robot the designer acts as the robot or user opposite the qounterpart. Can be done either 
in full size reinactment or with a simple prototype of play dough, cardboard, Little bits or more. In the process the three dimensions are discussed 
and the reinactment is repeated with the chosen interactive factors. 
Steps:
- Brainstorm on the types of interactions the robot and human will have. (A day in the life of Mr. Roboto)
- Build a simple prototype either small enough to hold in your hand or big enough to wear
- Reinact the predicted scenarios where the robot needs reaction patterns, while speaking out loud about what your doing and what steps the 
robot goes through
- Try limiting to one of the dimensions with blindfolds, earmuffs or restrains on your body/prototype, how does the objective express?
- Repeat with the corrections.
Additional thoughts
The culture is the biggest restain so the reinactmens should be framed as walk throughs and the restrictions as tests of some sort. As an alterna-
tive the ground/blueprint could be prototyped as well as the sound of the environment to simulate the surroundings even more. This could get 
the team to notice sertain restrictions in movement.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
The concept is based in basic prototyping tools and storyboarding techniques and lets you talk about the design while “in character” as the user or 
robot. A cheap and easy way to test out an interaction before you have a working prototype. 
_
+
Time efﬁcient
Prerequisites already on team?
Costs and investments
Novelty (Design, HRI, HCI)

A 7 2   |  A P P E N D I X  E  -  C O N C E P T U A L I S AT I O N
Concept No.  6
Designing a Cartoon Character
Date: 05.11.2015
Description
The method is about creating the perfect robot product, without thinking about the limitations of physics or technological abilities. The design 
team is asked to imagine a near future, 25 years from now. They are assigned with the task of creating the ideal solution to the problem in this 
setting. Now try to encapsule the core function/quality of the product by describing it in a three frames drawing. How does it solve the task. What 
does it look like? What does it sound like? How does it move?
The drawing sequence is later used to ask the questions of how can we make something as close as possible to this today? It can function as a 
source of inspiration to the actual design of the robot.
Purpose
The purpose of the this method is to open up the creative process of designing a robot, to cross boudaries and come up with novel designs. It can 
be used by design teams in the beginning of the design process, after the problem and needs have been established, but before a general 
concept has been desided upon. To use the method the design team needs a good understanding of the users and context. The output of the 
method the ideal concept that can work as inspiration for the further design process.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
Designs easily become restricted by what is possible today. It can be hard to think outside of the box. By putting aside these restictions the design 
team can open up for more creative innovative solutions. Later it might become apparent, that not everything from the dream is impossible. It 
might be that some of it can be incorporated already today. 
Additional thoughts
Inspiration can be found in Lowe’s Innovation Labs - Sci-Fi storytelling
-
+
Time efﬁcient
Prerequisites already on team?

D E V E LO P M E N T  O F  T O O L B OX  C O N TA I N I N G  M E T H O D S  F O R  H R I  D E S I G N   |   A 7 3
Concept No.  7
Dogmas
Date: 5. november 2015
Purpose
Helps you in the beginning of the project planning, as an initial step before visualizing the product or in determining the overall strategy for the 
company portfolio. Can also be used as a boundary object between designer and customer. Helps in getting from a deﬁned task with a clear user 
and useframe to a clear concept of a design with a holistic perspective ready to prototype and test. The objective is to avoid a self-contradicting 
sound, movement, appearance design.
Short description
By creating a set of abstract rules or dogmas the team can debate the different questions in relation to the overall vision of the product. This will 
end up with a more clear concept and brand position and could create a more holistic design for the robot or company portfolio.
Steps:
- Create a clear vision for the product: 
 
What sets this product apart? Where do you see it go? 
- Create rules/dogmas: 
 
Which rules/dogmas would help the vision along? Where do you need to provide further restriction?
- Continue with development of concept by ideation and conceptualization.
- Go through the prediﬁned questions to make sure the rules are followed in the chosen concept: 
 
Does the sound design live up to the desired vision? Does the appearance? Does the movements?
Additional thoughts
A clear concept of a design with a holistic perspective ready to prototype and test.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
The concept is based in theory where it seems clear that restrictions create a more focused and creative mindset and a uniﬁed vision for the team 
of where the concept is going.
_
+
Time efﬁcient
Prerequisites already on team?

A 74   |  A P P E N D I X  E  -  C O N C E P T U A L I S AT I O N
Concept No.  8
Icon Storyboarding
Date: 5. november 2015
Purpose
Help you in the movement, sound and appearance design, as a creative cleariﬁcation tool. Helps you get from a range of interactions to a concrete 
movement, sound or appearance gesture. The objective is to clearify the robots expressions.
Short description
By either having a range of icons you piece together an interaction. Afterwards the interaction objective is clariﬁed and the movements are cut 
down to only the very necissary pieces. 
Steps:
- Deﬁne a sequence of an interaction
- Deﬁne it in emojies
- Close your eyes, how would the sequence sound?
- Translate the emojies to functions 
- Create a function-means tree to translate the functions into means
Make sure through the process to only use the functions from the emojies and not add extra to the interaction
Additional thoughts
The goals of these storyboarding processes are not yet deﬁned. Maybe it should be made by already known icons, maybe with homemade ones, 
maybe from the emojies in an ipad and maybe it is just very clear drawings with one simple act. The difference between appearance and 
movements needs to be clearer deﬁned since emojies both can have “feelings” and “movements” in one.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
The concept is based in theory of sound from the idea that piecing together a language that is easy to translate into code and is known to both 
user and designer.
_

D E V E LO P M E N T  O F  T O O L B OX  C O N TA I N I N G  M E T H O D S  F O R  H R I  D E S I G N   |   A 7 5
Concept No.  9
Proof Your Concept - A boardgame in ideation to creation
Date: 5. november 2015
Purpose
Help you in the movement, sound and appearance design, as a creative provocation tool to get you out of your comfortzone and come up with 
novel ideas. Helps you integrate best practice concepts from theory in movement, sound and appearance. The objective is to create novel ideas 
with integrated known best practice principles.
Short description
A boardgame is played by the design team. In the game pieces with each of the 12 animation principles and known sound and appearance best 
practices are given to each player. When going through a process of ideation methods, everywhere in the process the players can thow a piece 
down to “challenge” the designer in either one of the best practice principle to make sure all the practices are thought of. The boardgame is a 
proces going through user analysis, problem brainstorm and storyboarding, initial open idea brainstorm, negative brainstorm, turn of the 
negative brainstorm, choice of the best 5 ideas, conceptualization, choice of 1 or more ideas, detailing and so on. 
Must have accessories:
- Storyboard made from individual squares of whiteboard pieces with whiteboard pens
- Concept test questions (if fail go back to concept and userintegrations ideation)
- Challenge cards with tests that the idea must contain
- LEGO or playdough
- Voting pieces of either “In favor” and “Against” or just green and red or voting panel numbers
Additional thoughts
This might be too silly, but i belive it would generate a lot of ideas and let the concept be tested with methods rather sooner than later.
Mechanism (Why will it work?)
The concept is based in motivation and contains a lot of methods tested by both concept generation in general and speciﬁc robot principles.
 Gamiﬁcation.
_
+

==PAGE:219==
G 
==PAGE:220==
Most design processes have a cyclic nature. They are not linear, but include the possibility to have several itterations 
starting from different points in the process.
O v e r a l l  t h e  d e s i g n  p r o c e s s e s  g o  t h r o u g h  s i m i l a r  s t e p s :
1.	
First there is a scoping face, where the subject is explored. The designer tries to understand the context, 
identify problems and clarify goals. 
2.	
Next some design processes involve some 
kind of analysis stage. This can include 
mapping of the context, stakeholders, 
experience etc. or determining the products 
functions and subfunctions, setting 
requirements and so forth.
3.	
Otherwise the next step is to explore the 
solution space. A lot of designs are generated 
and solutions invented.
4.	
Most processes emphasis prototyping the 
best designs next. Building the possible 
solutions help exploring the designs further.
5.	
Finaly the last step is to evaluate the designs. 
This can be through heuristics or user tests. 
The designs are measured on the quality 
T H E  F O L LO W I N G  A P P E N D I X  W I L L  LO O K  O N  S O M E  O F  T H E  M O ST  U S E D 
STA N D A R D  D E S I G N  M O D E L S  T O  I D E N T I F Y  T H E  G E N E R I C  STA G ES  O F  A  D E S I G N 
P R O C ES S .  T H E S E  STA G E S  W I L L  B E  U S E D  T O  I D E N T I F Y  T H E  STA G ES  O F 
D E V E LO P M E N T  I N  T H E  P R O J E C T S  O F  T H E  R O B O T I C  D E V E LO P E R S .
THE STANDARD DESIGN

and designers can learn from the evaluation as  a starting point for the next iteration, either going back and 
redefining the scope, the analysis or the design. 
It seams that the difference between interaction design processes and other processes is, that there is an increased 
focus on quick itterations, exploring details of the design.
With our project we wish to come up with methods for step 2 - 5, but the overall process will stay the same.

A P P E N D I X  H  -  F U L L  PA G E  F I G U R E S
figure H–24.	
THE NEXT STEPS TOWARDS DOMESTICATION OF THE HRI TOOLBOX
==PAGE:255==
This project aims to bridge the gab between knowledge obtained in 
Human-Robot Interaction research and the practice of developing robots 
in industry. The approach has been to map current research as well as 
development processes in Danish robotic companies to be able to identify 
specific needs and opportunities for new Human-Robot Interaction design 
methods. Several methods were developed through workshops with 
students and professionals and collected in a cohesive toolbox describing 
the useflow and purpose.
